The Sixth Proof: Following Abu Bakr and Umar
Cites the hadith 'Follow those after me' and responds to the Shi'i objection of it being a solitary report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof for the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar based on the prophetic command to follow them, and the response to the Shia objection that the hadith is a solitary report.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command to follow Abu Bakr and Umar is a valid proof, even if a solitary report, as Shia themselves use such reports.

The author presents a sixth proof for the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar: the Prophet's explicit command to follow them. The Shia object that this hadith is only a solitary report, not suitable for certainty. But in their response, the author points out the inconsistency of the Shia, who rely on solitary reports when it suits them. This lesson examines the hadith, the objection, and the rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its implication
Read the hadith where the Prophet commands following Abu Bakr and Umar. Note that even the weakest interpretation of a command implies permissibility.
2
Understand the Shia objection
The Shia argue that this hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and cannot be used for certainty in doctrinal matters. Consider why this objection might seem strong.
3
See the author's response
The author points out that the Shia themselves use solitary reports like the hadith of the bird and the hadith of the station. He accuses them of double standards: claiming mutawatir for favorable reports and solitary for unfavorable.
This reveals an inconsistency in their methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس: قوله عليه السلام: «اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر وأقل مراتب الأمر الجواز قالت الشيعة: هذا خبر واحد فلا يجوز أن يتمسك به فيما يطلب فيه اليقين. قلنا: ليس أقل من خبر الطير الذي يستدلون به على الأفضلية كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى ولا من خبر المنزلة الذي مر وهم يدعون فيما يوافق مذهبهم التواتر وفيما يخالفه الآحاد تحكماً فلا يكون ذلك الادعاء مقبولاً.
The sixth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow those after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' And the minimum level of a command is permissibility. The Shia said: This is a solitary report (khabar wahid), so it is not permissible to adhere to it in matters requiring certainty. We said: It is not less than the report of the bird (khabar al-tayr) which they use as evidence for superiority, as will come, Allah willing, nor from the report of the station (khabar al-manzila) which has passed. And they claim, regarding what agrees with their school, that it is mutawatir, and regarding what contradicts it, that it is solitary (ahad), as an arbitrary judgment. So such a claim is not acceptable.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof, a hadith in which the Prophet commands following Abu Bakr and Umar. The author notes that even at the minimum level of a command, it indicates permissibility if not obligation. The Shia object that this is a solitary report (khabar wahid) and cannot be used for certainty. In response, the author argues that the Shia themselves use solitary reports like the 'hadith of the bird' (khabar al-tayr) for superiority and the 'hadith of the station' (khabar al-manzila) for Ali's status. The author accuses them of inconsistency: they claim reports favoring them are mutawatir and those against are solitary arbitrarily. Thus, their objection is invalid.

Key Terms
اقتدوا
خبر واحد
خبر الطير
خبر المنزلة
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Shia are consistent in their hadith criticism.
Correction: The author shows they double-standard, claiming mutawatir for favorable reports and solitary for unfavorable.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the Shia objection that the hadith 'Follow those after me' is a solitary report?
A) He accepts the objection and seeks other evidence
B) He argues the Shia use solitary reports themselves
C) He claims the hadith is actually mutawatir
D) He rejects the hadith entirely

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof for Abu Bakr and Umar is a prophetic command, and the Shia objection based on solitary report is invalid due to their inconsistent standards.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you consistent in applying the same standards of evidence to religious teachings you agree with and those you disagree with? What would it require of you to be truly impartial like the author demands?
?
Have you ever dismissed a truth because it contradicted your cherished beliefs, while readily accepting similar evidence when it supported your views? How will you guard against this self-deception starting today?
?
The Prophet explicitly commanded to follow Abu Bakr and Umar. Is your heart truly aligned with that command, or do you harbor reservations? What specific action can you take to more sincerely follow their example in your daily life?

The Thirty-Year Caliphate: A Prophetic Proof
Cites the hadith of thirty-year caliphate to affirm the first four caliphs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the thirty-year caliphate serves as a proof for the legitimacy of the first four caliphs.

Core Idea
The Prophet's hadith distinguishes thirty years of true caliphate from later kingship.

This lesson examines a hadith in which the Prophet explicitly limits the duration of caliphate after him to thirty years, after which it becomes kingship. The author of the text uses this as a clear proof that the first four caliphs—Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali—held legitimate authority. The passage is straightforward but carries significant theological weight in Sunni kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and interpretation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the phrasing of the hadith and the author's conclusion.
Notice the key phrase 'ثلاثون سنة' (thirty years).
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the terms 'خلافة' (caliphate) and 'ملك عضوض' (biting kingship) and understand their contrast as presented by the author.
The author uses these terms to define two distinct periods.
3
Understand the proof logic
Reflect on why the hadith is considered a clear proof: the Prophet's statement affirms the caliphate of the first four rulers and distinguishes them from later kings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع: قوله عليه السلام الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم ملكاً عضوضاً فقد حكم بأن القائمين بالأمر في مدة ثلاثين سنة بعده عليه السلام موصوفون بالخلافة عنه في أمر الدين وإعلاء كلمة الله وأن القائمين به بعدها من أهل الدنيا موصوفون بكونهم ملوكاً وذلك دليل ظاهر على صحة خلافة الخلفاء الأربعة.
The seventh: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Caliphate after me is thirty years, then a biting kingship.' So he ruled that those in authority in the period of thirty years after him, peace be upon him, are described as caliphs from him in the matter of religion and raising the word of Allah, and that those in authority after it from the people of this world are described as kings. And that is a clear proof of the validity of the caliphate of the four caliphs.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof, a hadith stating that the caliphate after the Prophet will last thirty years, after which it becomes kingship. The author interprets this as a clear distinction: the first thirty years (the period of Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali) constitute legitimate caliphate, while later rulers are kings. This directly supports the validity of the four rightly-guided caliphs' rule. The argument is straightforward: the Prophet affirmed their caliphate, so it is correct.

Key Terms

ملك عضوض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim the hadith refers only to the first three caliphs, excluding Ali.
Correction: The author includes Ali as the fourth caliph, counting the thirty years from the Prophet's death to the end of Ali's caliphate in 40 AH (approximately 29-30 years), thus all four are covered.

Checkpoint

A) Ten years
B) Twenty years
C) Thirty years
D) Forty years

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's declaration of a thirty-year caliphate directly validates the rule of the first four caliphs as true caliphs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

In your own life, do you find yourself seeking authority or influence for worldly gain (like kings) rather than for the sake of Allah and the deen (like caliphs)? What can you change today to align your intentions with true caliphate?
?
You have just read a prophetic proof that distinguishes between true religious leadership and worldly kingship. When you look at the state of Muslim leadership today, does it resemble the caliphate or the kingship? And more importantly, what is your role? Are you contributing to a revival of true caliphate in your character, or are you complacent with the kingship around you?

The Eighth Proof: Prayer Leadership Implies General Imamate
Proof by appointment and analogy for Abu Bakr's imamate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr as prayer leader during his final illness serves as a proof for Abu Bakr's general imamate.

Core Idea
The Prophet's appointment for prayer implies leadership in all affairs.

This lesson examines the eighth proof for Abu Bakr's imamate: the Prophet appointed him to lead prayer during his final illness. The argument uses analogy: if he is fit to lead the most important religious duty, he is fit to lead the entire community. The text is incomplete but the reasoning is clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the literal translation. Notice the incomplete ending—restore the implied conclusion in your mind.
The text breaks off at 'إذ لا' but the intended conclusion is obvious: no distinction between prayer and other matters.
2
Identify the key elements
Find three things: the action (appointment to prayer), the lack of dismissal, and the analogy from prayer to other affairs.
The word 'استخلف' means appoint as successor; 'ما عزله' means he did not dismiss him.
3
Understand the analogy
The proof argues that since Abu Bakr was chosen for the most important religious duty (prayer) and remained in that role, the same applies to political leadership. This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning).
This analogy was a standard argument for Abu Bakr's caliphate.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this proof was so persuasive to the early community: prayer was the core of Islam, so leadership in prayer was seen as proof of overall suitability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The eighth: That he, peace be upon him, appointed Abu Bakr as his successor in prayer during his illness, and he led them, and he did not dismiss him, as his determination has passed. So he remains after him an imam in it, and likewise in other matters, for there is no

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth proof: the Prophet appointed Abu Bakr to lead prayer during his final illness, and he led the Companions without being dismissed. Since prayer leadership is a form of imamate, and the Prophet's choice for the most important religious duty indicates suitability for general leadership, Abu Bakr should be the imam in all matters. The argument is by analogy (qiyas): what applies to prayer applies to other affairs. The text cuts off at 'for there is no...' but the intended conclusion is clear.

The Honor Proof for Abu Bakr's Caliphate
Abu Bakr's honor proves his imamate's validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the third proof for Abu Bakr's imamate uses the premise of divine honor to affirm his caliphate's validity.

Core Idea
Divine honor proves the validity of Abu Bakr's caliphate.

This lesson examines the third proof for the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's imamate. The argument is concise: if his caliphate were invalid, God would not have honored him; but we know from revelation and consensus that he is honored and the most virtuous after the Prophet, so his imamate must be true. This logical structure is common in kalam reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the conditional structure and the conclusion.
The passage is short but packs a complete argument.
2
Identify the three parts of the argument
Break the passage into: (1) the conditional premise, (2) the factual premise (Abu Bakr is honored), and (3) the implied conclusion (his imamate is valid).
3
Understand the logical flow
Recognize that the proof works by contrapositive: if the conclusion is false, the premise cannot hold. Since the premise (honor) is true, the conclusion must be true.
This is a standard proof by contradiction in kalam.
4
Consider the reference to 'afḍaliyya'
Notice the author mentions that the issue of superiority will be explained later. This indicates the proof relies on the established fact of Abu Bakr's superiority.
The later discussion will strengthen the premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : لو كانت إمامة أبي بكر باطلة لما كان أبو بكر معظماً عند الله لكنه معظم وأفضل الخلق عنده بعد رسول الله وسنزيده شرحاً في مسألة الأفضلية
Third: If the imamate of Abu Bakr were invalid, then Abu Bakr would not be honored by God, but he is honored and the best of creation with Him after the Messenger of God, and we will increase its explanation in the issue of superiority.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument for the validity of Abu Bakr's caliphate. It is a straightforward proof: it posits that if Abu Bakr's imamate were false, then God would not have honored him. Since we know from revelation and consensus that Abu Bakr is indeed honored and is the most virtuous of people after the Prophet, his imamate must be true. The passage also refers to a later discussion on the issue of superiority (al-afḍaliyya), indicating that the argument will be elaborated further. This is a typical kalam argument from divine approval.

Key Terms
إمامة
أفضلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular because it assumes Abu Bakr's honor to prove his imamate.
Correction: The proof is not circular; it uses an independent premise (Abu Bakr's honor from revelation and consensus) to deduce the validity of his imamate. The honor is not derived from the imamate but from divine texts.

Checkpoint
What does the third proof for Abu Bakr's imamate argue?
A) That Ali was more virtuous than Abu Bakr
B) That Abu Bakr's honor from God proves his caliphate's validity
C) That the caliphate is invalid
D) That Abu Bakr was not honored by God

Key Takeaway
The third proof uses divine honor as a sign that Abu Bakr's caliphate is valid and divinely approved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If you were in a position of authority, would you seek God's honor or people's approval? Which one matters more to you right now?
?
Are you willing to accept that God's honor of someone means you should honor them too, even if your own preferences differ? What holds you back from doing so?

Fourth Proof: The Companions' Address
A concise proof from the Companions' address and Quranic testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof for Abu Bakr's caliphate, which is based on the Companions' address and the Quranic testimony of their truthfulness.

Core Idea
The Companions' truthfulness, attested by the Quran, validates Abu Bakr's caliphate.

This lesson presents the fourth argument for Abu Bakr's imamate, drawn from the practice of the Companions. When the Companions, including Ali, addressed Abu Bakr as 'Caliph of the Messenger of God,' and the Quran testifies to their truthfulness, their affirmation establishes the legitimacy of his caliphate. We will examine the structure of this proof and its foundation in divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the concise structure: an action by the Companions, a Quranic verse, and a conclusion.
The verse reference is Surah al-Hashr, verse 8.
2
Identify the two premises
The proof has two premises: (1) The Companions and Ali called Abu Bakr 'Caliph of God's Messenger'. (2) God testifies that those Companions are truthful. Identify both in the text.
3
Connect the premises to the conclusion
The conclusion is that Abu Bakr's caliphate is true. How do the premises support this? Because truthful people cannot be mistaken about such a matter. Reflect on the logical link.
This is a direct inference from the Quranic praise.
4
Consider the objection and response
Some might argue that Ali's address was out of fear, not genuine acceptance. But the Quranic praise of the Companions' truthfulness counters this objection. Think about why this objection fails.
The objection is based on political circumstances, but the proof relies on divine testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: كانت الصحابة وعلي يقولون له : يا خليفة رسول الله وقد قال تعالى فيهم أولئك هم الصادقون [الحشر: ۸]، فتكون خلافته حقاً
Fourth: The Companions and Ali used to say to him: 'O Caliph of the Messenger of God,' and God Almighty said about them: 'Those are the truthful ones' [al-Hashr: 8], so his caliphate is true.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth argument for Abu Bakr's imamate. It is based on the practice of the Companions, including Ali ibn Abi Talib, who addressed Abu Bakr as 'O Caliph of the Messenger of God.' The proof argues that since the Quran testifies to the truthfulness of these Companions (referring to the verse in Surah al-Hashr), their acceptance and affirmation of Abu Bakr's caliphate must be correct. Therefore, his caliphate is established as true.

Key Terms
خليفة
الصادقون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that Ali's address to Abu Bakr was only out of fear or taqiyya, not genuine acceptance.
Correction: The proof relies on the Quran's general praise of the Companions' truthfulness, which encompasses Ali. If the Quran declares them truthful, their words cannot be dismissed as insincere.

The Ummah's Goodness as Proof of Caliphate
Sanusi presents the fifth proof, a reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio ad absurdum argument that uses the Quran's description of the ummah as the best of nations to defend the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Core Idea
If the ummah is the best, its choice of Abu Bakr must be right.

Sanusi presents the fifth argument for Abu Bakr's caliphate, a clever reductio ad absurdum. It starts with the opposing claim that Ali was the rightful imam but lacked community support. From that, it derives a contradiction with the Quran's praise of the ummah. This forces the conclusion that the community's actual choice—Abu Bakr—must be correct. Let's examine the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the concise structure: premise, consequence, Quranic rebuttal, conclusion.
2
Identify the logical form
This is a reductio ad absurdum: assume the opposite, derive a contradiction, then reject the assumption.
The assumption is that Ali was rightful imam but ummah didn't support him.
3
Connect to the Quranic verse
The argument relies on the Quran calling the ummah 'the best nation' (خير أمة). Find that phrase and understand its weight.
Surah Aal-e-Imran 3:110 is the reference.
4
Reflect on the strength and limits
Consider why this argument is persuasive for Sunnis and how Shi'a might respond (e.g., the ummah went astray).
The common misunderstanding highlights the sectarian nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : لو كانت الإمامة حق علي ولم تعنه الأمة عليه ) كما تزعمون ( لكانوا شر الأمم لكنهم خير أمة يأمرون بالمعروف وينهون عن المنكر، كما دل عليه نص القرآن
Fifth: If the imamate were the right of Ali and the community did not assist him upon it, as you claim, they would be the worst of nations, but they are the best nation, enjoining good and forbidding evil, as the text of the Quran indicates.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument for Abu Bakr's caliphate. It is a reductio ad absurdum: If Ali were the rightful imam but the community (umma) failed to support him, then the umma would be the worst of nations. However, the Quran explicitly describes this umma as the best of nations, commanding good and forbidding evil. Therefore, the premise that Ali was the rightful imam without the community's support must be false, implying that the community's choice of Abu Bakr was correct.

Key Terms
خير أمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument proves the ummah is infallible and its consensus is always correct.
Correction: The argument only shows that the ummah could not have collectively rejected the true imam while being described as the best; it does not assert infallibility in all matters.

Checkpoint
What does the fifth proof conclude about the ummah?
A) It is the best of nations, so its support of Abu Bakr is correct
B) It is the worst of nations for not supporting Ali
C) The ummah has no role in choosing the imam
D) Ali was the rightful imam despite lack of support

Key Takeaway
The Quran's praise of the ummah as 'best of nations' is used to argue that their collective choice of Abu Bakr over Ali must have been correct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson argues that the Ummah's goodness proves their choice of Abu Bakr was correct. Do you trust the collective decisions of the Muslim community today? When have you doubted the community's judgment in matters of religion? How does this argument challenge your own inclinations to question the historical consensus?
?
The Quran calls the Ummah 'the best nation' because they enjoin good and forbid evil. Is that true of your own actions? Do you enjoin good and forbid evil in your daily life, or do you remain silent? What would change if you took this description literally?
?
Sanusi uses a logical proof to defend the caliphate. How comfortable are you with using reason and logic to defend matters of faith? Are there aspects of your belief where you rely solely on emotion or tradition rather than rational conviction? Will you examine them?

Hadith of Following Abu Bakr and 'Umar: Proof and Response
A hadith proof for imamate with Shi'a objection and Sunni response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Sunni defenders respond to the Shi'a objection regarding the hadith 'Follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar' by pointing out inconsistency in accepting single-transmission reports.

Core Idea
The Shi'a objection backfires when applied consistently.

This passage presents the sixth argument for Abu Bakr's imamate: the Prophet's command to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar. The Shi'a object that the hadith is a single-transmission report, but the Sunni response exposes an inconsistency in the Shi'a own acceptance of similar reports. Let's examine this exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three parts: the hadith proof, the Shi'a objection, and the Sunni response.
The Arabic uses technical terms: khabar wahid, tawatur, ahad.
2
Identify the proof and objection
What is the main argument from the hadith? What is the Shi'a objection? Write them down in your own words.
The objection is based on the hadith being a single-transmission report.
3
Analyze the response
How does the Sunni response counter the objection? What specific examples do they cite? Why is this an effective rebuttal?
The key is pointing out the Shi'a inconsistency with hadith al-tayr and hadith al-manzila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : قوله عليه السلام : «اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر» وأقل مراتب الأمر الجواز قالت الشيعة : هذا خبر واحد فلا يجوز أن يتمسك به فيما يطلب فيه اليقين. قلنا : ليس أقل من خبر الطير الذي يستدلون به على الأفضلية كما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى ولا من خبر المنزلة الذي مر وهم يدعون فيما يوافق مذهبهم التواتر وفيما يخالفه الآحاد تحكماً فلا يكون ذلك الادعاء مقبولاً
Sixth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow those after me: Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' The least degree of the command is permissibility. The Shi'a said: This is a single-transmission report (khabar wāḥid), so it is not permissible to adhere to it in matters requiring certainty. We said: It is not less than the hadith of the bird (khabar al-ṭayr) which they use as evidence for superiority, as will come, nor than the hadith of the station (khabar al-manzila) which has passed. And they claim, in what agrees with their school, that it is widely transmitted (tawātur), and in what contradicts it, that it is single-transmission (āḥād), arbitrarily; so that claim is not acceptable.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof for Abu Bakr's imamate, which is the prophetic hadith commanding the community to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar after the Prophet. The argument notes that the least level of a command is permissibility, implying the legitimacy of their leadership. However, the Shi'a object that this hadith is a single-transmission report (khabar wāḥid) and cannot be used for matters requiring certainty like imamate. The response counters that the Shi'a themselves rely on single-transmission reports, such as the hadith of the bird (about Ali's superiority) and the hadith of the station (about Ali being like Aaron to Moses), when it suits them. They inconsistently claim tawātur when evidence supports their view and dismiss it as āḥād when it contradicts them. Thus, their objection is rejected.

Key Terms
خبر واحد
خبر الطير
خبر المنزلة
تواتر
آحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the hadith is weak or unreliable, and that is why the Shi'a reject it.
Correction: The issue is not the reliability of the hadith per se, but the Shi'a inconsistent standard: they accept similar single-transmission reports when it supports their view.

Checkpoint
How do the Sunni defenders respond to the Shi'a objection that the hadith 'Follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar' is a single-transmission report?
A) They admit it is weak but still usable
B) They point out that the Shi'a themselves use single-transmission reports like the hadith of the bird
C) They claim it is mutawatir
D) They ignore the objection

Key Takeaway
The Sunni response to the Shi'a objection hinges on exposing the inconsistency in accepting single-transmission reports when they support one's own view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever rejected a clear command from Allah or His Prophet because it demanded something inconvenient, just as the Shi'a dismissed this hadith when it contradicted their position? What would it cost you to follow it today?
?
Where in your own life do you apply double standards—accepting evidence that flatters your desires and rejecting what challenges them? Can you name one area where you need to be more consistent?
?
The Prophet commanded you to follow Abu Bakr and 'Umar. Do you truly honor them in your heart and speech? If not, what is holding you back from submitting to this instruction?

Imamate of 'Umar: Established by the Text of Abu Bakr
The author presents the explicit text of Abu Bakr's will appointing 'Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the imamate of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab is legitimately established through the explicit appointment (naṣṣ) by Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, and why this is considered a valid method in Sunni doctrine.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's explicit appointment of 'Umar provides a clear textual basis for his caliphate.

In this lesson, we examine the second caliph 'Umar's accession to leadership. The author explains that while some previous proofs apply generally, the primary evidence for 'Umar is the direct text (naṣṣ) from Abu Bakr. We will read the actual wording of Abu Bakr's will and understand why it is considered a binding designation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage noting the shift from general proofs to specific method
Notice how the author first mentions that some of the earlier proofs (verses and hadiths) can also support the imamate of the three caliphs, then focuses specifically on 'Umar's case. This sets the context for the main evidence.
The general proofs include the verse about believers and the hadith of 'the caliphate after me'.
2
Identify the content of Abu Bakr's will and its significance
Find the quoted text of the will. It shows Abu Bakr's explicit designation of 'Umar as his successor. Note the language of covenant and the reference to 'Umar's good conduct.
The will is written by 'Uthman ibn 'Affan at Abu Bakr's order.
3
Reflect on why naṣṣ is a valid method for establishing imamate
Consider that in Sunni theology, an explicit appointment by the previous caliph is a legitimate way to determine succession, as seen here with Abu Bakr and 'Umar.
This contrasts with the shura method used for the later caliphs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب إمامة الأئمة الثلاثة تعلم ما يثبت منها ببعض الوجوه المذكورة يريد أن ما ذكرناه إنما كان لإثبات إمامة أبي بكر وأما إمامة الأئمة الثلاثة الباقية فأنت تعلم أنها أو بعضاً منها يمكن إثباتها ببعض الوجوه السابقة مثل قوله تعالى : وعد الله الذين آمنوا [النساء : ٩٥] الآية، وقوله عليه السلام : «الخلافة بعدي » الحديث وقوله : «اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي» إلى آخره وطريقه المعول عليه في حق عمر نص أبي بكر وذلك أنه دعا في مرضه عثمان بن عفان وأمره أن اكتب : هذا ما عهد أبو بكر بن أبي قحافة آخر عهده من الدنيا وأول عهده بالعقبى حالة فيها الفاجر ويؤمن فيها الكافر إني استخلفت عليكم عمر بن الخطاب فإنه حسن السيرة فذلك ظني به والخير أردت وإن تكن الأخرى فسيعلم الذين ظلموا أي منقلب ينقلبون [الشعراء: ۲۲۷]، وفي حق عثمان وعلي البيعة فإنه لا ينص على أحد بل جعل الإمامة شورى بين ستة وهم عثمان وعلي وعبد الرحمن بن عوف وطلحة والزبير وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وقال : لو كان أبو عبيدة بن الجراح حيا لما ترددت فيه. وإنما جعلها شورى بينهم لأنه رآهم أفضل ممن عداهم وأنه لا يصلح للإمامة غيرهم وقال في حقهم مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو عنهم راض، ولم يترجح في نظره واحد منهم فأراد أن يستظهر برأي غيره في التعيين ولذلك قال : إن انقسموا اثنين وأربعة فكونوا مع الأربعة ميلا منه إلى الأكثر لأن رأيهم إلى الصواب أقرب وإن تساووا فكونوا في الحزب الذي فيه عبد الرحمن، ولم يصل للصلاة عليه كيلا يفهم منه أنه عينه بل وصى بها إلى صهيب، ولما تشاوروا اتفقوا على عثمان وبايعه عبد الرحمن. ولما استشهد عثمان اتفق الناس على بيعة علي رضي الله تعالى عنه
Appendix: The imamate of the three imams. You know what is established from it by some of the mentioned ways. He means that what we have mentioned was only to prove the imamate of Abu Bakr. As for the imamate of the remaining three imams, you know that it, or some of it, can be established by some of the previous ways, such as His saying: 'God has promised those who believe...' [al-Nisa: 95] verse, and his saying, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me' hadith, and his saying: 'Follow those after me' to the end. And its reliable method concerning 'Umar is the text (naṣṣ) of Abu Bakr. That is, during his illness he called 'Uthman ibn 'Affan and ordered him to write: 'This is what Abu Bakr ibn Abi Quhafa has covenanted at the end of his life from the world and the beginning of his life in the afterlife, in a state in which the wicked believes and the disbeliever believes: I have appointed over you 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, for he is good in conduct. That is my opinion of him, and I intend good. If he does otherwise, then the oppressors will know what end they will meet.' [al-Shu'ara: 227]. And concerning 'Uthman and 'Ali, it is by pledge of allegiance (bay'a). For he did not explicitly nominate anyone, but made the imamate a council (shūrā) among six: 'Uthman, 'Ali, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. He said: 'If Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah were alive, I would not have hesitated about him.' He made it a council because he considered them superior to others and that no one else was suitable for the imamate. He said about them: 'The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, died while being pleased with them.' And none of them was preponderant in his view, so he wanted to seek the opinion of others in the appointment. Therefore, he said: 'If they divide into two and four, then be with the four,' inclining toward the majority because their opinion is closer to correctness. 'If they are equal, then be in the party that includes 'Abd al-Rahman.' And he did not appoint anyone to lead the prayer over him so that it would not be understood that he had designated him; rather, he entrusted it to Suhayb. When they consulted, they agreed upon 'Uthman, and 'Abd al-Rahman gave him the pledge. When 'Uthman was martyred, the people agreed upon the pledge of allegiance to 'Ali, may God be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage is an appendix (tadhneeb) explaining how the imamate of the three remaining caliphs—'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali—is established. It begins by noting that some of the previous proofs used for Abu Bakr (such as the verse about believers, the hadith of thirty-year caliphate, and the hadith of following) can also be applied to the others. Then it specifies the primary method for each. For 'Umar, it is the explicit appointment (naṣṣ) by Abu Bakr, who dictated a will during his illness designating 'Umar as his successor. The passage quotes the text of that will. For 'Uthman and 'Ali, the method is election (bay'a) through a council (shūrā) set up by 'Umar on his deathbed. The passage details the composition of the council and the reasoning behind it, including 'Umar's instructions to favor the majority and the role of 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf. It also mentions that 'Umar did not appoint a prayer leader to avoid implying a designation. The council eventually agreed on 'Uthman, and after his death, the people pledged allegiance to 'Ali. Thus, the imamate of all four caliphs is justified by either explicit appointment (for Abu Bakr and 'Umar) or by consensus/election (for 'Uthman and 'Ali).

Key Terms
نص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'Umar's caliphate lacked legitimate basis because it was not through shura.
Correction: The passage shows that explicit appointment by the preceding caliph (naṣṣ) is a recognized method; Abu Bakr's will provides clear textual evidence.

Checkpoint
How was 'Umar's imamate established according to this passage?
A) By the Prophet's explicit text
B) By Abu Bakr's appointment (naṣṣ)
C) By election through shura
D) By popular acclaim

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's explicit text (naṣṣ) is the primary evidence for 'Umar's legitimate caliphate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a critical decision that affects others, do you articulate your intentions as clearly and openly as Abu Bakr did in his will, or do you leave room for ambiguity? What would it take for you to be that explicit?
?
The will states that both the wicked and the disbeliever believe at the moment of death. Are there truths you are avoiding now that you know will become unavoidable later? What is preventing you from facing them today?
?
Abu Bakr based his appointment on 'Umar's conduct and his own best judgment, then entrusted the outcome to God. In your own responsibilities, do you take care to choose based on merit and transparency, or do you rely on convenience and silence your conscience?

Imamate of 'Uthman and 'Ali: Established by Shura and Bay'a
The author describes the shura instituted by 'Umar and the subsequent bay'a for 'Uthman and 'Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the imamate of 'Uthman and 'Ali was established through the council (shūrā) set up by 'Umar and the subsequent pledge of allegiance (bay'a), and the reasoning behind this process.

Core Idea
The shura mechanism for selecting 'Uthman and the subsequent bay'a for 'Ali demonstrate legitimate succession through consultation and consensus.

This lesson covers the transfer of power after 'Umar. Instead of appointing a successor, he formed a council of six leading Companions to decide. We will examine the composition of the shura, 'Umar's instructions, and how it led to the election of 'Uthman, and later the pledge to 'Ali after 'Uthman's martyrdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the shura and its members
Notice that 'Umar did not nominate anyone but selected six prominent Companions: 'Uthman, 'Ali, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas.
He considered them the best of the remaining Companions.
2
Note 'Umar's reasoning for choosing these six
He believed they were the most qualified and that no one else was suitable. He also mentioned that the Prophet died pleased with them.
3
Observe the decision process and how the council agreed on 'Uthman
'Umar gave instructions: if the council splits into two and four, choose the four; if equal, choose the party with 'Abd al-Rahman. After consultation, they all agreed on 'Uthman, and 'Abd al-Rahman gave him the pledge.
This shows a preference for majority and reliance on 'Abd al-Rahman's judgment.
4
Understand how 'Ali became caliph after 'Uthman
After 'Uthman's martyrdom, the people unanimously pledged allegiance to 'Ali. This shows a different process: consensus of the community.
Both processes are considered valid in Sunni doctrine.

?

?

?
'Umar trusted the judgment of 'Abd al-Rahman in case of a tie. Is there someone in your life whose judgment you trust enough to follow in uncertainty? If not, why not? If yes, when was the last time you actually deferred to them, and what held you back?

The Most Virtuous After the Prophet: The Proof from Surah al-Layl
A proof from Quran 92:17 that Abu Bakr is the most virtuous after the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school uses Quran 92:17 to argue that Abu Bakr is the most virtuous person after the Prophet Muhammad.

Core Idea
The verse about 'the most righteous' was revealed about Abu Bakr, so he is the most virtuous.

This lesson explores a key proof in Sunni theology for the superiority of Abu Bakr after the Prophet. The debate over who is most virtuous – Abu Bakr or 'Ali – has deep historical roots. Here, the Ash'ari position grounds its argument in a Quranic verse that exegetes traditionally associate with Abu Bakr. By examining this proof, you will see how scriptural interpretation supports a major theological claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two opposing views presented at the beginning.
2
Identify the positions
The passage states the Ash'ari/early Mu'tazila view (Abu Bakr) and the Shi'a/later Mu'tazila view ('Ali). Understand that this is a sectarian debate.
The proof that follows is for the Sunni position.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Layl (92:17) is cited. Note how it is interpreted: 'the most righteous' (al-atqā) is said to be Abu Bakr, and being most righteous implies being most honorable (akram).
This is a direct link between the verse and the claim of superiority.
4
Reflect on the argument
Ask yourself: Why does the author rely on the interpretation of exegetes? How does this establish virtue? Consider the logical step from 'atqā' to 'afḍal'.
The argument assumes that righteousness translates to honor before God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الخامس : الأفضل بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في أفضل الناس بعد رسول الله هو عندنا وأكثر قدماء المعتزلة أبو بكر رضي الله عنه، وعند الشيعة وأكثر متأخري المعتزلة علي لنا وجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : وسيجنبها الأتقى الذي يؤتي ماله يتزكى [الليل : ۱۸]، قال أكثر المفسرين وقد اعتمد عليه العلماء إنها نزلت في أبي بكر فهو أتقى ومن هو أتقى فهو أكرم
Fifth Objective: The Most Virtuous After the Messenger of God, peace be upon him. Concerning the most virtuous of people after the Messenger of God: according to us (the Ash'aris) and most of the early Mu'tazila, it is Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him. According to the Shi'a and most of the later Mu'tazila, it is 'Ali. We have proofs: First, His saying, exalted is He: 'And the most righteous will be spared it, who gives his wealth to purify himself' [al-Layl: 18]. Most of the exegetes, and the scholars have relied upon it, say that it was revealed about Abu Bakr. So he is the most righteous (atqā), and whoever is most righteous is most honorable (akram).
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage introduces the fifth objective (al-maqṣad al-khāmis) of this section, which is to determine who is the most virtuous (al-afḍal) after the Prophet. It states the Sunni (Ash'ari) position and the position of early Mu'tazila that Abu Bakr is most virtuous, while the Shi'a and later Mu'tazila hold that 'Ali is most virtuous. Then it begins to present proofs, starting with the first proof: the verse from Surah al-Layl: 'And the most righteous will be spared it...' Most exegetes and scholars hold that this verse was revealed about Abu Bakr. Therefore, Abu Bakr is the most righteous (atqā), and being most righteous implies being most honorable (akram) before God. This establishes his superiority over others.

Key Terms
الأفضل
الأتقى
أكرم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some groups, particularly among the Shi'a, deny that this verse refers to Abu Bakr, arguing it is general or refers to someone else.
Correction: The Ash'ari position depends on the majority of exegetes and scholars who affirm that the verse was specifically revealed about Abu Bakr, thus establishing his supreme righteousness.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof for Abu Bakr being the most virtuous after the Prophet?
A) A hadith praising Abu Bakr
B) The verse 'And the most righteous will be spared it' interpreted as referring to Abu Bakr
C) The consensus of the Companions
D) The practice of the Umayyads

Key Takeaway
The first proof for Abu Bakr's superiority is the Quranic verse 'And the most righteous will be spared it', which exegetes interpret as referring to Abu Bakr, thus establishing him as the most virtuous after the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verse promises that the most righteous will be spared the Fire. Abu Bakr gave his wealth for purification. Are you giving of your wealth and time in a way that purifies you, or are you holding back? What would it take for you to be among those who are 'spared'?
?
This lesson asserts that superiority is based on righteousness, not lineage or popularity. Who in your life do you truly honor? Is it based on their piety or on worldly status? Challenge yourself to examine your real criteria.
?
The proof relies on accepting the interpretation of the majority exegetes. Are you willing to submit your personal opinions to the consensus of scholars, even when it contradicts your preferences? Where in your faith are you resistant to this?

The First Proof: The Most Righteous is Abu Bakr
The first proof: Quranic evidence for Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verses from Surah al-Layl (92:17-19) are used as a proof for Abu Bakr's superiority over Ali.

Core Idea
The Quran names Abu Bakr as the most righteous, and the most righteous is the most excellent.

In this lesson, we examine the first proof presented by the author for the position that Abu Bakr is the most excellent after the Prophet. The proof relies on a specific Quranic passage and the principle that righteousness (taqwā) determines honor before Allah. We will see how the author deduces Abu Bakr's superiority and why Ali is excluded.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic passage
Read the verses from Surah al-Layl (92:17-19) carefully. Notice that they describe a person who is 'most righteous' and who gives his wealth to purify himself, and that no one has a favor to be rewarded.
The phrase 'the most righteous' (al-atqā) is key.
2
Identify the interpretation
The author states that most commentators held that this verse was revealed about Abu Bakr. Accept this as given and note the consequence: Abu Bakr is the most righteous.
3
Apply the principle
Using another verse (49:13), the most righteous is the most honorable before Allah, and the most honorable is the most excellent. Thus Abu Bakr is the most excellent.
This is a logical deduction.
4
Consider the exclusion of Ali
The author argues that the following verse (92:19) about having no favor to be rewarded prevents the verse from applying to Ali because Ali had the favor of being raised by the Prophet. Therefore, the verse must refer to Abu Bakr.
This is based on consensus that the most righteous is either Abu Bakr or Ali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الخامس : الأفضل بعد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ] لم في أفضل الناس بعد رسول الله هو عندنا وأكثر قدماء المعتزلة أبو بكر رضي الله عنه، وعند الشيعة وأكثر متأخري المعتزلة علي ( لنا وجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : وسيجنبها الأتقى الذي يؤتى ماله يتزكى ﴾ [الليل : ۱۸]، قال أكثر المفسرين و) قد اعتمد عليه العلماء إنها نزلت في أبي بكر فهو أتقى ومن هو أتقى فهو ( أكرم عند الله لقوله تعالى : وإن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم ﴾ [ الحجرات : ١٣] وهو) أي : الأكرم عند الله هو ( الأفضل ) فأبو بكر أفضل ممن عداه الأمة وأيضاً فقوله: من وما لأحد عنده من نعمة تجزى ﴾ [الليل : ۱۹] يصرفه عن ) الحمل على ( علي إذ ١٩] عنده نعمة التربية ) فإن النبي ربى علياً ) وهي نعمة تجزى ) وإذا لم يحمل عليه تعين أبو بكر للإجماع على أن ذلك الأتقى هو أحدهما لا غير ( الثاني قوله عليه السلام: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر ، عمم الأمر بالاقتداء ( فيدخل في الخطاب علي وهو يشعر بالأفضلية إذ لا يؤمر الأفضل ولا المساوي بالاقتداء سيما عندهم) إذ لا يجوزون إمامة المفضول أصلا كما سيأتي .
The Fifth Objective: The most excellent after the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. [Some said] As for the most excellent person after the Messenger of Allah, according to us and most of the early Mu'tazila, it is Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him. According to the Shia and most of the later Mu'tazila, it is Ali. We have proofs: First: His saying, 'And the most righteous will be removed from it, he who gives his wealth to purify himself' [Quran 92:17-18]. Most commentators and scholars have relied on it that it was revealed about Abu Bakr, so he is the most righteous. And whoever is the most righteous is the most honorable before Allah, because of His saying, 'Indeed, the most noble of you in the sight of Allah is the most righteous of you' [Quran 49:13]. And the most honorable before Allah is the most excellent. So Abu Bakr is more excellent than all others of the community. Also His saying, 'And no one has with him any favor to be rewarded' [Quran 92:19] prevents it from being applied to Ali, because Ali has the favor of upbringing from the Prophet, and that is a favor to be rewarded. And if it is not applied to him, then Abu Bakr is determined by consensus that that most righteous is one of them only. Second: His (peace be upon him) saying, 'Follow those after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' He generalized the command to follow, so it includes Ali, and it implies superiority, because the superior or the equal is not commanded to follow, especially according to them, for they do not allow the imamate of the inferior as will come.
Source pages p. 397

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth maqṣad (objective) regarding who is the most excellent (afḍal) after the Prophet Muhammad (SAW). The author states the position of the Ahl al-Sunna and most early Mu'tazila that it is Abu Bakr, while the Shia and later Mu'tazila say it is Ali. Then he gives the proofs (wujūh). The first proof is the Quranic verse (92:17-18) about the most righteous (al-atqā) who gives his wealth. The majority of commentators said it was revealed about Abu Bakr, so he is the most righteous. Then using the verse (49:13) that the most honorable is the most righteous, he concludes that Abu Bakr is the most honorable and thus the most excellent. He also argues that the following verse (92:19) about having no favor to be rewarded prevents the verse from applying to Ali because Ali had the favor of being raised by the Prophet. Therefore, the verse must refer to Abu Bakr. The second proof is the hadith, 'Follow those after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' The command to follow (iqtidā') is general, including Ali. It implies superiority because a superior or equal is not commanded to follow, especially according to the opponents (the Shia) who do not allow the imamate of the inferior.

Key Terms
الأتقى
الأفضل
الاقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the verse about the most righteous could apply to Ali because of his generosity and piety.
Correction: The author argues that the following verse about having no favor to be rewarded excludes Ali because he had the favor of being raised by the Prophet, so the verse must refer to Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why does the verse 'And no one has with him any favor to be rewarded' exclude Ali?
A) Because Ali was not generous
B) Because Ali had a favor from the Prophet (upbringing)
C) Because the verse was not revealed about anyone
D) Because the verse refers to a different person

Key Takeaway
The Quranic proof for Abu Bakr's superiority relies on identifying him as the most righteous and then deducing that the most righteous is the most excellent before Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If this passage convinces you that Abu Bakr is the most righteous, what does that mean for how you view your own pursuit of righteousness? Is your striving based on seeking honor from Allah alone, or are you held back by favors and expectations from others? This week, identify one act of worship you will do solely for Allah's sake, without any sense of entitlement.
?
The passage excludes Ali because he had a favor from the Prophet. Reflect on a favor someone has done for you. Do you feel that favor gives you a 'claim' on them or on Allah? How can you purify your deeds so that your good actions are not tainted by a sense of obligation? Commit to performing a secret act of charity or service this week that no one knows about.
?
The argument here uses the principle that the most righteous is the most honorable. Evaluate your life: what are you actually pursuing to increase your honor? Is it through material status or through taqwa? What is one concrete change you need to make today to align your priorities with this Quranic truth?

The Second Proof: The Hadith of Following Abu Bakr and Umar
The second proof: Hadith evidence for Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's command to follow Abu Bakr and Umar implies their superiority over all others, including Ali.

Core Idea
The Prophet commanded even Ali to follow Abu Bakr and Umar, proving their excellence.

The second proof is a hadith in which the Prophet instructs the community to follow Abu Bakr and Umar after him. The author argues that this command implies superiority because a superior or equal is not commanded to follow an inferior, especially according to the Shia who do not allow the imamate of the inferior. We will see how this argument is constructed.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the hadith: 'Follow those after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' Note that it is a command to follow (iqtidā').
The hadith is general, including all companions.
2
Understand the implication
The command to follow implies that Abu Bakr and Umar are superior to those who are commanded to follow them. This is because a superior or equal is not commanded to follow an inferior.
This logic is based on the principle of imamate.
3
Apply to Ali
Since Ali is included in the command (he is one of the companions), he is commanded to follow Abu Bakr and Umar. Therefore, they are superior to him.
4
Consider the opponents' view
The author notes that especially according to the Shia, who do not allow the imamate of the inferior, this proof is strong. They must accept that Abu Bakr and Umar are superior since the Prophet would not command following an inferior.
This strengthens the argument against the Shia position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Fifth Objective: The most excellent after the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. [Some said] As for the most excellent person after the Messenger of Allah, according to us and most of the early Mu'tazila, it is Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him. According to the Shia and most of the later Mu'tazila, it is Ali. We have proofs: First: His saying, 'And the most righteous will be removed from it, he who gives his wealth to purify himself' [Quran 92:17-18]. Most commentators and scholars have relied on it that it was revealed about Abu Bakr, so he is the most righteous. Objections and Answers on the Second and Third Proofs for Abu Bakr's Superiority
Responds to Shi'a objections on the second proof's reasoning and the third hadith, and explains the fourth proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni scholars addressed Shi'a objections to the proofs of Abu Bakr's superiority, using principles of language, custom, and logic.

Core Idea
Theological arguments must address both literal and customary interpretations.

This passage from the commentary responds to several objections raised against the proofs for Abu Bakr's superiority. It clarifies a nuance in the second proof, refutes two Shi'a objections to the hadith of Abu ad-Darda', and explains a potential confusion about the phrase 'masters of the elders of Paradise.' Studying these responses reveals the careful reasoning underlying Sunni kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the three distinct issues discussed.
2
Identify the three issues
Notice the comment on the second proof, the two objections on the third hadith, and the clarification of the fourth proof.
Each issue is based on a different part of the original text.
3
Examine the use of custom (urf)
See how the commentator argues that customary understanding overrides literal language in the first objection.
This is a key tool in Islamic legal and theological reasoning.
4
Understand the principle of no time-restriction
The second objection is refuted by the principle that unqualified statements are not limited in time.
This principle is common in usul al-fiqh.
5
Reflect on the fourth proof clarification
The commentator shows that 'masters of the elders of Paradise' does not contradict hadiths saying the people of Paradise are young.
This resolves an apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إذ لا يؤمر الأفضل إلخ لعل هذا إلزامي إذ يجوز عندنا إمامة المفضول كما سيجيء إلا أن قوله : سيما عندهم يشعر بأن ما قبله على عمومه ففيه ما فيه . قوله : ( الثالث قوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم لأبي الدرداء إلخ) اعترض عليه الشيعة بأن الحديث المذكور لا يدل على أنه أفضل بل على أن غيره ليس أفضل منه فيجوز أن يكون مساوياً له وبأنه يجوز أن يكون أيضاً بحسب وقت أي يكون الأفضل عند ورود هذا الخبر هو وبعد ذلك يكون غيره أفضل منه والجواب عن الأول : أن مفهوم هذا الخبر بحسب اللغة وإن كان أن غيره ليس أفضل منه إلا أن مفهومه بحسب العرف أنه أفضل من غيره لأنه حيث يقال : ليس في هذا البلد أحد أفضل من فلان يفهم كل أحد أنه أفضل أهله والعرف إذا عارض اللغة كان الترجيح للعرف وأيضاً يروى أن أبا الدرداء كان يمشي أمام أبي بكر رضي الله عنهما فقال صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم : ( أيمشي أمام من هو خير منك فقال أبو الدرداء : أهو خير مني، فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : والله ما طلعت إلخ . فهذه القصة تدل على أن المراد أفضليته مطلقاً لا مساواته كما لا يخفى. وعن الثاني : أن تقييده بالوقت خلاف الأصل لأن الأصل عدم التقييد . قوله: (سيدا كهول أهل (الجنة أي سيدا الكهول الذين يدخلون الجنة ولا يلزم منه كون بعض أهل الجنة كهول الجنة حين كونه في الجنة حتى يشكل بقوله عليه السلام : «أهل الجنة جرد مرد».
His saying: (Since the superior is not commanded... etc.) Perhaps this is a necessitating argument because in our view the leadership of the inferior is permissible, as will come, except that his saying: 'especially according to them' suggests that what preceded it is general, so there is something in it. His saying: (Third: His saying, may God exalt him and give him peace, to Abu ad-Darda' etc.) The Shi'a objected that the mentioned hadith does not indicate that he is more excellent, but rather that another is not more excellent than him, so it is possible that he is equal to him; and also that it could be according to time, i.e., he is the most excellent at the time of this report, and after that someone else could be more excellent. The answer to the first: The implication of this report according to language, although it is that another is not more excellent than him, but according to custom its implication is that he is more excellent than others, because when it is said: 'There is no one in this town more excellent than so-and-so,' everyone understands that he is the most excellent of its people. And custom, when it conflicts with language, is given preference. Also it is narrated that Abu ad-Darda' was walking in front of Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with them, and the Prophet, may God exalt him and give him peace, said: 'Are you walking in front of one who is better than you?' Abu ad-Darda' said: 'Is he better than me?' Then the Prophet said: 'By Allah, the sun has not risen... etc.' This story indicates that the intent is his absolute superiority, not equality, as is not hidden. As for the second: Limiting it to time is contrary to the principle, for the principle is the absence of limitation. His saying: (The two masters of the elders of Paradise) meaning the two masters of the elders who enter Paradise, and it does not necessitate that some of the people of Paradise are elders at the time they are in Paradise, so as to be problematic with his saying, peace be upon him: 'The people of Paradise are young beardless youths.'
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage contains two marginal comments addressing objections. The first comment discusses the point in the second proof about the command to follow—the commentator notes that the author's reasoning might be necessitarian, and that in Sunni doctrine the leadership of the inferior is permissible, so the objection is not strong. The second and longer comment addresses a Shi'a objection to the third proof (the hadith to Abu ad-Darda'). The Shi'a claim the hadith only says no one is better than him, which leaves room for equality, and that it might be time-specific. The answer uses two arguments: first, customary understanding (ʿurf) overrides literal language; second, the story of Abu ad-Darda' walking in front of Abu Bakr confirms absolute superiority. The second objection is answered by the principle that unqualified statements are absolute. Finally, there is a brief explanation of the phrase 'masters of the elders of Paradise' from the fourth proof, clarifying that it does not imply elders remain elders in Paradise.

Key Terms
شيعة
عرف
لغة
أفضل
مساواة
تقييد بالوقت
كهول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a hadith saying 'no one is better than him' only indicates equality, not superiority.
Correction: The passage shows that customary usage and a supporting story demonstrate that such phrasing implies absolute superiority.

Checkpoint
What is the first objection of the Shi'a regarding the hadith to Abu ad-Darda'?
A) The hadith is weak
B) The hadith only indicates non-superiority, not superiority
C) The hadith is specific to a time
D) The hadith is fabricated

Key Takeaway
Customary understanding and the principle of no time restriction are essential tools for interpreting hadiths in Sunni theological argumentation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone described as 'the best' in a religious context, do you automatically start looking for flaws to reduce their standing? How does the custom-based interpretation in this lesson challenge your inner tendency to diminish those whom Allah has elevated?
?
Is there a command from the Prophet that you have quietly restricted to a 'time and place' to avoid applying it to yourself? What would it cost you to accept it as unrestricted and binding on you today?
?
The Prophet corrected Abu Darda for walking ahead of one better than him. In your daily life, are you walking ahead of someone better—perhaps in knowledge, piety, or age—without proper deference? What concrete step can you take to realign your behavior?

Six Proofs for Abu Bakr's Superiority
Lists six proofs from Quran and hadith for Abu Bakr's superiority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand six distinct proofs from the Quran and hadith that Sunni scholars use to establish the superiority of Abu Bakr over the rest of the Ummah after the Prophet.

Core Idea
Six textual proofs establish Abu Bakr's superiority over the entire Ummah.

This passage presents six distinct proofs drawn from the Quran and authentic hadith for the superiority of Abu Bakr. The author lists them in a logical order, each building on the previous. Before examining these proofs, it's helpful to understand the nature of the argument: the claim is that Abu Bakr is the best of the Ummah after the Prophet, and these proofs are meant to demonstrate that through scripture and consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Get a sense of the rhythm and the list-like structure.
Notice that each proof begins with a new indicator like 'the second' or 'the sixth'.
2
Identify each proof and its source
Go through the passage and identify all six proofs. For each, note whether it comes from the Quran or a hadith, and what the key argument is.
3
Analyze how each proof argues for superiority
For each proof, consider what it shows about Abu Bakr. For example, the first uses two verses to argue he is the most righteous. The second uses a command to follow him as an indication of superiority over those commanded to follow.
The sixth proof is an event rather than a direct statement.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Think about why establishing superiority matters. The passage is part of a larger discussion on the caliphate and the virtues of the Companions.
These proofs are used to support the Sunni position on the caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد الخامس : الأفضل بعد رسول الله عند الله لقوله تعالى : وإن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم ﴾ [ الحجرات : ١٣] وهو) أي : الأكرم عند الله هو ( الأفضل ) فأبو بكر أفضل ممن عداه الأمة وأيضاً فقوله: من وما لأحد عنده من نعمة تجزى ﴾ [الليل : ۱۹] يصرفه عن ) الحمل على ( علي إذ ١٩] عنده نعمة التربية ) فإن النبي ربى علياً ) وهي نعمة تجزى ) وإذا لم يحمل عليه تعين أبو بكر للإجماع على أن ذلك الأتقى هو أحدهما لا غير ( الثاني قوله عليه السلام: اقتدوا بالذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر ، عمم الأمر بالاقتداء ( فيدخل في الخطاب علي وه وهو يشعر بالأفضلية إذ لا يؤمر الأفضل ولا المساوي بالاقتداء سيما عندهم) إذ لا يجوزون إمامة المفضول أصلا كما سيأتي . ( الثالث : قوله عليه السلام لأبي الدرداء : والله ما طلعت شمس ولا غربت بعد النبيين والمرسلين على رجل أفضل من أبي بكر . الرابع: قوله عليه السلام لأبي بكر وعمر هما سيدا كهول أهل الجنة ما خلا النبيين والمرسلين». الخامس : قوله عليه السلام : « ما ينبغي لقوم فيهم أبو بكر أن يتقدم عليه غيره . السادس : تقديمه في الصلاة مع أنها أفضل العبادات، وقوله : ( يأبى الله ورسوله إلا أبا بكر وفي معناه قوله : يأبى المسلمون إلا أبا بكر وذلك أن بلالاً أذن بالصلاة في أيام مرضه فقال النبي عليه السلام لعبد الله بن زمعة: «اخرج وقل لأبي بكر يصلي بالناس فخرج فلم يجد على الباب إلا عمر في جماعة ليس فيهم أبو بكر، فقال : يا عمر صل بالناس فلما كبر وكان رجلاً صيتاً وسمع عليه السلام صوته قال ذلك ثلاث مرات.
The Fourth Observation - The Fifth Purpose: The Most Excellent after the Messenger of Allah. (He is) according to God's saying: 'Indeed the most noble of you in the sight of God is the most righteous' [al-Hujurat 13] and He is, meaning the most honorable with God, is the most excellent. So Abu Bakr is more excellent than the rest of the Ummah. And also His saying: 'And who has upon him no favor to be recompensed' [al-Layl 19] diverts it from being applied to 'Ali because he has the favor of upbringing, for the Prophet raised 'Ali, and it is a favor to be recompensed. And if it is not applied to him, then Abu Bakr is determined because of the consensus that that most righteous is one of them and no other. The second: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' He made the command to follow general, so 'Ali enters into the address, and this intimates superiority, because the superior or the equal is not commanded to follow, especially according to them, since they do not permit the leadership of the inferior, as will come. The third: His saying, peace be upon him, to Abu ad-Darda': 'By Allah, the sun has not risen nor set after the prophets and messengers upon a man more excellent than Abu Bakr.' The fourth: His saying, peace be upon him, regarding Abu Bakr and 'Umar: 'They are the masters of the elders of Paradise, aside from the prophets and messengers.' The fifth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'It is not fitting for a people among whom is Abu Bakr that anyone else should precede him.' The sixth: His advancement in prayer, although it is the best of acts of worship, and His saying: 'God and His Messenger refuse except Abu Bakr,' and similar to it is his saying: 'The Muslims refuse except Abu Bakr.' That is because Bilal called the prayer during his illness, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, said to 'Abdullah ibn Zam'a: 'Go out and tell Abu Bakr to lead the people in prayer.' So he went out and found only 'Umar at the door among a group, and Abu Bakr was not among them. So he said: 'O 'Umar, lead the people in prayer.' When he said the takbir and was a man with a loud voice, and the Prophet, peace be upon him, heard his voice, he said that three times.
Source pages p. 398

Commentary
This passage presents six proofs for the superiority of Abu Bakr over the entire Ummah after the Prophet. The first proof uses two Quranic verses: 'Indeed the most noble of you is the most righteous' and 'and who has upon him no favor to be recompensed.' The argument is that Abu Bakr is the most righteous, whereas 'Ali cannot be meant by the second verse because he had the favor of being raised by the Prophet, which is a favor to be recompensed. Thus the most righteous must be Abu Bakr. The second proof is the hadith 'Follow those after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar.' Since following is commanded and the one followed is superior, and since 'Ali is included in the command, it implies Abu Bakr's superiority over 'Ali. The third proof is the explicit hadith to Abu ad-Darda' stating no one after the prophets is more excellent than Abu Bakr. The fourth proof says Abu Bakr and 'Umar are masters of the elders of Paradise. The fifth says it is not fitting for a people with Abu Bakr that anyone else precede him. The sixth proof describes the event of the Prophet commanding Abu Bakr to lead the prayer despite the presence of 'Umar and others, indicating his precedence. The passage follows the order of the proofs as listed by the author.

Key Terms
أفضل
أبو بكر
عمر
علي
أتقى
القدوة
الخلفاء
الصلاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali is superior to Abu Bakr because of his close relationship to the Prophet.
Correction: The Quranic verse (al-Layl 19) indicates that the most righteous is one who has no favor to be recompensed. 'Ali had the favor of being raised by the Prophet, so he cannot be the one intended, leaving Abu Bakr as the most righteous.

Checkpoint
Which proof uses the verse 'Indeed the most noble of you is the most righteous'?
A) The first proof
B) The second proof
C) The third proof
D) The sixth proof

Key Takeaway
The six proofs demonstrate a consistent scriptural basis for the Sunni belief in Abu Bakr's superiority over the Ummah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet insisted on Abu Bakr leading prayer even when others were present. When have you insisted on your own preference over what the Prophet clearly indicated? How can you train yourself to submit to his choices?
?
If you were to truly internalize that Abu Bakr is the most excellent after the Prophet, would it change the way you view the early Muslim community? Would it challenge any biases or attachments you have?
?
The command to 'follow those after me, Abu Bakr and 'Umar' is a direct order. Are you consciously trying to follow their example in your daily life? What specific steps can you take to emulate their character?

Four Proofs for Abu Bakr's Superiority
Lists four proofs with commentary on khalil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four specific proofs (7th–10th) presented for Abu Bakr's superiority over other companions, including the hadith of khalil and Ali's testimony.

Core Idea
Explicit hadiths and Ali's own words establish Abu Bakr's preeminence.

This lesson covers the seventh to tenth proofs for Abu Bakr's superiority as compiled by al-Iji. These include two explicit prophetic hadiths, a detailed praise of Abu Bakr, and a crucial testimony from Ali ibn Abi Talib himself. We also explore the meaning of 'khalil' in the eighth proof, clarifying a potential misunderstanding about the Prophet's relationship with Abu Bakr.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice that it lists four proofs, each introduced by a number (seventh, eighth, etc.) and ends with a commentary on the word 'khalil'.
2
Identify each proof and its source
The seventh proof is the hadith 'The best of my community is Abu Bakr, then Umar.' The eighth is the hadith about not taking a khalil besides his Lord. The ninth is a longer hadith praising Abu Bakr's support. The tenth is a saying of Ali.
Each proof has a different character: explicit ranking, special closeness, detailed merits, and a companion's endorsement.
3
Understand the explanation of 'khalil'
The commentary explains that 'khalil' means a sincere companion one relies on for needs. The Prophet says if he were to take such a friend from creation, it would be Abu Bakr, but his ultimate reliance is on Allah.
This clarifies that the hadith does not imply any form of partnership with Allah.
4
Reflect on the significance of Ali's testimony
Ali's saying that the best after prophets are Abu Bakr and Umar, and his trust that God will unite people on their best, is a powerful counter to Shi'a claims. Note how the author references 'the Shi'a' in the commentary.
This proof is particularly important in intra-Muslim debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(السابع : قوله عليه السلام : (خير أمتي أبو بكر ثم عمر . الثامن : قوله عليه السلام: «لو كنت متخذاً خليلاً دون ربي لاتخذت أبا بكر خليلاً ولكن هو شريكي في ديني وصاحبي الذي أوجبت له صحبتي في الغار وخليفتي في أمتي التاسع : قوله عليه السلام وقد ذكر عنده أبو بكر ) ( وأين مثل أبي بكر كذبني الناس وصدقني وآمن بي وزوجني ابنته وجهزني بماله وواساني بنفسه وجاهد معي ساعة الخوف العاشر : قول علي رضي الله عنه : خير الناس بعد النبيين أبو بكر ثم عمر ثم الله اعلم. وقوله : إذ قيل :له ما توصي؟ أي أما توصي وما تعين من يقوم مقامك بعدك ( ما أوصى رسول الله حتى أوصي ولكن إن أراد الله بالناس خيراً جمعهم على خيرهم كما جمعهم بعد نبيهم على خيرهم لهم أي للشيعة ومن وافقهم. قوله: (لو كنت متخذاً خليلاً الحديث الخليل : الصاحب الواد الذي يفتقر إليه ويعتمد عليه في الأمور فإن أصل التركيب للحاجة والمعنى لو كنت متخذاً من الخلق خليلاً أراجع إليه الحاجات وأعتمد عليه في المهمات لاتخذت أبا بكر ولكن الذي أجلاً إليه وأعتمد عليه في جملة الأمور ومجامع الأحوال هو الله تعالى .
(Seventh: His saying, peace be upon him: 'The best of my community is Abu Bakr, then 'Umar.' Eighth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'If I were to take a close friend besides my Lord, I would have taken Abu Bakr as close friend, but he is my partner in my religion and my companion to whom I have made his company obligatory in the cave, and my successor in my community.' Ninth: His saying, peace be upon him, when Abu Bakr was mentioned before him: 'And where is the like of Abu Bakr? The people denied me, but he confirmed me, believed in me, married his daughter to me, equipped me with his wealth, supported me with himself, and strove with me in the hour of fear.' Tenth: The saying of 'Ali, may God be pleased with him: 'The best of people after the prophets is Abu Bakr, then 'Umar, then God knows best.' And his saying when it was said to him: 'Do you not recommend? Do you not appoint someone to stand in your place after you?' (I did not recommend as the Messenger of God recommended, but if God intends good for the people, He will unite them upon the best of them, just as He united them after their Prophet upon the best of them.) This is for the Shi'a and those who agree with them. His saying: (If I were to take a close friend...) the close friend is the sincere companion to whom one turns for needs and relies upon in matters; the root of the construction indicates need. The meaning: If I were to take from creation a close friend to whom I return for needs and rely upon in important matters, I would have taken Abu Bakr, but the One to Whom I turn and upon Whom I rely in all matters and all states is God Almighty.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage lists four more proofs for Abu Bakr's superiority. The seventh is the explicit hadith that the best of the community is Abu Bakr then 'Umar. The eighth is the famous hadith about al-khalīl (intimate friend), where the Prophet states that if he were to take a close friend besides his Lord, he would take Abu Bakr, and then lists his special roles. The ninth proof recounts the Prophet's praise of Abu Bakr for his support, belief, marriage, wealth, and companionship. The tenth proof is the testimony of 'Ali himself that Abu Bakr and 'Umar are the best, and his refusal to appoint a successor, trusting that God will unite the people on their best, as He did after the Prophet. The marginal comment explains the meaning of 'khalīl' in the eighth hadith, emphasizing the idea of reliance and need.

Key Terms
خير أمتي
خليلاً
خليفتي
علي
الشيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith of 'khalil' implies that Abu Bakr is a partner in divinity or equal to the Prophet in some way.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that 'khalil' means a sincere companion one relies on for needs; the Prophet's ultimate reliance is on Allah. The hadith emphasizes Abu Bakr's closeness without compromising tawhid.

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'khalil' in the eighth proof according to the commentary?
A) Friend
B) Successor
C) Helper
D) Companion

Key Takeaway
The four proofs together establish Abu Bakr's superiority through prophetic hadiths and Ali's own testimony, with the khalil explanation reinforcing its theological soundness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said he would take Abu Bakr as a close friend if not for his exclusive reliance on Allah. Is there any human being in your life whom you trust so much that you depend on them more than you depend on Allah? What would it take to shift that trust entirely to Allah while still loving that person for His sake?
?
Ali, despite being passed over for the caliphate, publicly declared Abu Bakr and Umar as the best after the prophets. Do you have the humility to acknowledge the excellence of those you may feel were unjustly preferred over you? Where in your life are you holding onto resentment instead of trusting God’s wisdom in placing others above you?
?
In the hour of fear, Abu Bakr stood by the Prophet when others denied him. When your faith is tested, are you among those who stand firm and support the truth, or do you retreat into silence and self-preservation? What concrete step will you take this week to be a 'companion in the cave' to someone in need?
